					<h1 id="section_0">Johnson &amp; Johnson</h1>

			<div id="bodyContent" class="content"><div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="mw-parser-output"><section class="mf-section-0" id="mf-section-0"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/S._C._Johnson_%26_Son" title="S. C. Johnson &amp; Son">S. C. Johnson &amp; Son</a>.</div>

<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>
<p><b>Johnson &amp; Johnson</b> is an American <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational corporation</a> founded in 1886 that develops medical devices, pharmaceutical and consumer packaged goods. Its common stock is a component of the <a href="/wiki/Dow_Jones_Industrial_Average" title="Dow Jones Industrial Average">Dow Jones Industrial Average</a> and the company is ranked No. 37 on the 2018 <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> list of the largest United States corporations by total revenue. J&amp;J is one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_public_corporations_by_market_capitalization" title="List of public corporations by market capitalization">world's most valuable companies</a>.

href="https://www.jnj.com">www<wbr></wbr>.jnj<wbr></wbr>.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table><p>Johnson &amp; Johnson is headquartered in <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick,_New_Jersey" title="New Brunswick, New Jersey">New Brunswick, New Jersey</a>, the consumer division being located in <a href="/wiki/Skillman,_New_Jersey" title="Skillman, New Jersey">Skillman, New Jersey</a>. The corporation includes some 250 subsidiary companies with operations in 60 countries and products sold in over 175 countries. Johnson &amp; Johnson had worldwide sales of $70.1 billion during calendar year 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup>
Johnson &amp; Johnson's brands include numerous household names of medications and <a href="/wiki/First_aid" title="First aid">first aid</a> supplies. Among its well-known consumer products are the <a href="/wiki/Band-Aid" title="Band-Aid">Band-Aid</a> Brand line of bandages, <a href="/wiki/Tylenol_(brand)" title="Tylenol (brand)">Tylenol</a> medications, <a href="/wiki/Johnson%27s_Baby" title="Johnson's Baby">Johnson's Baby</a> products, <a href="/wiki/Neutrogena" title="Neutrogena">Neutrogena</a> <a href="/wiki/Cosmetics" title="Cosmetics">skin and beauty products</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clean_%26_Clear" title="Clean &amp; Clear">Clean &amp; Clear</a> facial wash and <a href="/wiki/Acuvue" title="Acuvue">Acuvue</a> <a href="/wiki/Contact_lens" title="Contact lens">contact lenses</a>.
</p>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(1)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnson_%26_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History" data-section="1" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-1 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-1">
<p>Johnson &amp; Johnson operates over 250 companies in what is termed "the Johnson &amp; Johnson family of companies".<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> The company operates in three broad divisions; Consumer Healthcare, Medical Devices and Pharmaceuticals.
</p>
<table class="wikitable"><tbody><tr><th colspan="3"><small>Johnson &amp; Johnson Family of Companies</small>
</th></tr><tr><th>Consumer Healthcare<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></th>
<th>Medical Devices<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></th>
<th>Pharmaceuticals<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></th></tr><tr><td>Baby Care<br>Skin &amp; Hair Care<br>Wound Care and Topicals<br>Oral Health Care<br>Women's Health<br>McNeil Consumer Healthcare<br>Over-The-Counter Medicines<br>Nutritionals</td>
<td><br>Biosense Webster<br><a href="/wiki/DePuy" title="DePuy">DePuy Synthes</a><br><a href="/wiki/Ethicon,_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="Ethicon, Inc.">Ethicon, Inc.</a><br>Janssen Diagnostics BVBA<br>Johnson &amp; Johnson Vision Care, Inc.<br><br>Mentor</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Janssen_Pharmaceutica" title="Janssen Pharmaceutica">Janssen</a><br>Janssen R&amp;D LLC<br>Janssen Healthcare Innovation<br>Janssen Pharmaceuticals Inc<br>Janssen Diagnostics<br><a href="/wiki/Janssen_Therapeutics" class="mw-redirect" title="Janssen Therapeutics">Janssen Therapeutics</a><br>Janssen Scientific Affairs<br>McNeil-PPC, Inc
</td></tr></tbody></table><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Foundation_and_early_history">Foundation and early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnson_%26_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Foundation and early history" data-section="2" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Robert-wood-johnson-i.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Robert-wood-johnson-i.jpg/180px-Robert-wood-johnson-i.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="232" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="988"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 180px;height: 232px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Robert-wood-johnson-i.jpg/180px-Robert-wood-johnson-i.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="180" data-height="232" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Robert-wood-johnson-i.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Robert Wood Johnson</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Johnson_and_Johnson_corrosive_sublimate_cotton.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Johnson_and_Johnson_corrosive_sublimate_cotton.jpg/220px-Johnson_and_Johnson_corrosive_sublimate_cotton.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="125" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="362" data-file-height="206"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 125px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Johnson_and_Johnson_corrosive_sublimate_cotton.jpg/220px-Johnson_and_Johnson_corrosive_sublimate_cotton.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="125" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Johnson_and_Johnson_corrosive_sublimate_cotton.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Early corrosive sublimate cotton packaging with the signature logo</div></div></div>
<p>Inspired by <a href="/wiki/Antiseptic" title="Antiseptic">antiseptic</a> advocate <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Lister,_1st_Baron_Lister" class="mw-redirect" title="Joseph Lister, 1st Baron Lister">Joseph Lister</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Wood_Johnson_I" title="Robert Wood Johnson I">Robert Wood Johnson</a> joined his brothers, <a href="/wiki/James_Wood_Johnson" title="James Wood Johnson">James Wood Johnson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Edward_Mead_Johnson" title="Edward Mead Johnson">Edward Mead Johnson</a>, to create a line of ready-to-use <a href="/wiki/Dressing_(medical)" title="Dressing (medical)">surgical dressings</a> in 1885. The company produced its earliest products in 1886. Those products initially featured a logo that resembled the signature of James Wood Johnson, very similar to the logo used today.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (February 2020)">better source needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>Robert Wood Johnson served as the first president of the company. Upon his death in 1910, he was succeeded in the presidency by his brother James Wood Johnson until 1932, and then by his son, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Wood_Johnson_(son)" class="mw-redirect" title="Robert Wood Johnson (son)">Robert Wood Johnson II</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>Robert Wood Johnson's granddaughter, <a href="/wiki/Mary_Lea_Johnson_Richards" title="Mary Lea Johnson Richards">Mary Lea Johnson Richards</a>, was the first baby to appear on a Johnson &amp; Johnson baby powder label.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="1943-44:_Credo_and_Going_Public">1943-44: Credo and Going Public</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnson_%26_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1943-44: Credo and Going Public" data-section="3" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 1943, as the company was preparing for its <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">initial public offering</a> (IPO), Robert Wood Johnson wrote what would become called by the company "Our Credo," a defining document that has been used to guide the company's decisions over the years.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> The company completed its IPO and became a <a href="/wiki/Public_company" title="Public company">public company</a> in 1944.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="1959:_McNeil_Consumer_Healthcare">1959: McNeil Consumer Healthcare</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnson_%26_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1959: McNeil Consumer Healthcare" data-section="4" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>McNeil Consumer Healthcare was founded on March 16, 1879, by Robert McNeil. In 1904, one of McNeil's sons, Robert Lincoln McNeil, became part of the company, and together they created McNeil Laboratories in 1933. The company focused on the <a href="/wiki/Direct_marketing" title="Direct marketing">direct marketing</a> of prescription drugs to hospitals, pharmacists, and doctors. The development of <a href="/wiki/Acetaminophen" class="mw-redirect" title="Acetaminophen">acetaminophen</a> began under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Robert_L._McNeil,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Robert L. McNeil, Jr.">Robert L. McNeil, Jr.</a>, who later served as the firm's chairman. In 1959, Johnson &amp; Johnson acquired McNeil Laboratories and a year later, the company was able to sell <a href="/wiki/Tylenol_(brand)" title="Tylenol (brand)">Tylenol</a> for the first time without a prescription.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p><p>In 1977, two subsidiary companies were created: McNeil Medicals Products and McNeil Consumer Products Company (also known as McNeil Consumer Healthcare). In 1993, McNeil Medicals Products merged with <a href="/wiki/Ortho_Pharmaceutical" title="Ortho Pharmaceutical">Ortho Pharmaceutical</a> to form <a href="/wiki/Ortho-McNeil_Pharmaceutical" title="Ortho-McNeil Pharmaceutical">Ortho-McNeil Pharmaceutical</a>. In 2001, McNeil Consumer Healthcare changed its name to McNeil Consumer &amp; Specialty Medicals Products. The name was later changed to "McNeil Consumer Healthcare".<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="1959:_Cilag">1959: Cilag</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnson_%26_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1959: Cilag" data-section="5" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 1933, Swiss chemist <a href="/wiki/Bernhard_Joos" title="Bernhard Joos">Bernhard Joos</a>, set up a small research laboratory in <a href="/wiki/Schaffhausen" title="Schaffhausen">Schaffhausen</a>, Switzerland.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> This led to the founding of Chemische Industrie-Labor AG (Chemical Industry Laboratory AG or Cilag) on 12 May 1936.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In 1959, Cilag joined Johnson &amp; Johnson.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In the early 1990s, the marketing departments of Cilag and <a href="/wiki/Janssen_Pharmaceutica" title="Janssen Pharmaceutica">Janssen Pharmaceutica</a> joined to form Janssen-Cilag.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The non-marketing departments still operate under their original name.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="1961:_Janssen_Pharmaceuticals">1961: Janssen Pharmaceuticals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnson_%26_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1961: Janssen Pharmaceuticals" data-section="6" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 1933, <a href="/wiki/Constant_Janssen" title="Constant Janssen">Constant Janssen</a>, the father of Paul Janssen, acquired the right to distribute the pharmaceutical products of <a href="/wiki/Gedeon_Richter_Ltd." class="mw-redirect" title="Gedeon Richter Ltd.">Richter</a>, a Hungarian pharmaceutical company, for Belgium, the Netherlands and <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Congo" title="Belgian Congo">Belgian Congo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-17">[17]</a></sup> On 23 October 1934, he founded the N.V. Produkten Richter in <a href="/wiki/Turnhout" title="Turnhout">Turnhout</a>. After the Second World War, the name was changed to Eupharma, although the original company name Richter would remain until 1956.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-18">[18]</a></sup></p><p>In 1956, Paul Janssen founded his own research laboratory within the Richter-Eurpharma company of his father. On 5 April 1956, the name of the company was changed to NV Laboratoria Pharmaceutica C. Janssen (named after Constant Janssen).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> On 2 May 1958, the research department in Beerse became a separate legal entity known as the N.V. Research Laboratorium C. Janssen. On 24 October 1961, the company was acquired by the American corporation Johnson &amp; Johnson.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:1_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-17">[17]</a></sup></p><p>On 10 February 1964, the name was changed to Janssen Pharmaceutica N.V.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-18">[18]</a></sup> In 1999, clinical research and non-clinical development became a global organization within Johnson &amp; Johnson.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In 2001, a portion of their research activities were transferred to the United States and reorganized under the <a href="/wiki/Johnson_%26_Johnson_Pharmaceutical_Research_and_Development" title="Johnson &amp; Johnson Pharmaceutical Research and Development">Johnson &amp; Johnson Pharmaceutical Research and Development</a> organization.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The research activities of the Janssen Research Foundation and the R.W. Johnson Pharmaceutical Research Institute were merged into the new global research organization.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> On 27 October 2004, the Paul Janssen Research Center was founded.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>In August 2013, the company acquired Aragon Pharmaceuticals, Inc.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> In November 2014, the company acquired Alios BioPharma, Inc. for $1.75 billion. As a result of the purchase, Alios was incorporated into the infectious diseases therapeutic area of Janssen Pharmaceuticals.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="1998:_DePuy">1998: DePuy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnson_%26_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 1998: DePuy" data-section="7" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/DePuy" title="DePuy">DePuy</a> was acquired by J&amp;J in 1998, rolling it into the Johnson &amp; Johnson Medical Devices group.
</p><p>In September 2010, Johnson &amp; Johnson announced it had completed the acquisition of Micrus Endovascular, manufacturer of minimally invasive devices for hemorrhagic and ischemic strokes. Micrus will operate under Codman Neurovascular, a business unit of Codman &amp; Shurtleff, Inc.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p><p>On June 14, 2012, Johnson and Johnson completed the acquisition of <a href="/wiki/Synthes" title="Synthes">Synthes</a> for $19.7 billion,<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> which was then integrated with the DePuy franchise to establish the DePuy Synthes Companies of Johnson &amp; Johnson which includes: Codman &amp; Shurteff, Inc., DePuy Mitek, Inc., DePuy Orthopaedics, Inc. and DePuy Spine, Inc. In February 2015, DePuy announced it would acquire Olive Medical Corporation.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> In May 2016, DePuy Orthopaedics, Inc. acquired Biomedical Enterprises, Inc., an industry leader in small bone fixation.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> Later in December of the same year, DePuy Synthes announced it would acquire Pulsar Vascular Inc., adding Pulsar to its Codman division.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p><p>In January 2017, the company acquired Interventional Spine, Inc.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> In April 2017, Irish subsidiary DePuy Ireland Unlimited Company announced it would acquire Neuravi, a company with a portfolio of products for hemorrhagic and ischemic strokes for an undisclosed sum, with Codman Neuro being behind the deal.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> In June, DePuy Synthes Products, Inc. announced it would acquire Innovative Surgical Solutions, LLC (trading as Sentio, LLC) for an undisclosed sum, bolstering the company's technology for innovative nerve localisation in spinal surgery.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="1999:_Janssen_Biotech.2C_Inc."></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1999:_Janssen_Biotech,_Inc.">1999: Janssen Biotech, Inc.</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnson_%26_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 1999: Janssen Biotech, Inc." data-section="8" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Janssen Biotech, Inc., formerly known as Centocor Biotech, Inc., is a biotechnology company that was founded in <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a> in 1979. In 1982, Centocor transitioned into a publicly traded company. In 1999, Centocor became a wholly owned subsidiary of Johnson &amp; Johnson. Since the acquisition, Janssen Biotech increased its annual sales from $500 million to more than $2 billion. During the same period, research and development investment increased from $75 million to more than $300 million.
</p><p>In 2008, Centocor, Inc. and Ortho Biotech Inc. merged to form Centocor Ortho Biotech Inc. In June 2009 Johnson &amp; Johnson, through a new wholly owned subsidiary, Kite Merger Sub, Inc., announced it would purchase all outstanding shares of common stock of Cougar Biotechnology, Inc. for $43.00 in cash or around $970 million.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> In the same year, Johnson &amp; Johnson Nordic AB acquired Amic, developer of in vitro diagnostic, further strengthening the Ortho-Clinical Diagnostics division.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p><p>In June 2010, Centocor Ortho Biotech acquired RespiVert, a privately held <a href="/wiki/Drug_discovery" title="Drug discovery">drug discovery</a> company focused on developing small-molecule, inhaled therapies for the treatment of pulmonary diseases.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> In June 2011, Centocor Ortho Biotech changed its name to Janssen Biotech, Inc. as part of a global effort to unite the Janssen Pharmaceutical Companies around the world under a common identity. In December 2014, the company announced it would co-develop MacroGenics cancer drug candidate (MGD011) which targets both <a href="/wiki/CD19" title="CD19">CD19</a> and <a href="/wiki/CD3_(immunology)" title="CD3 (immunology)">CD3</a> proteins in treating <a href="/wiki/B-cell" class="mw-redirect" title="B-cell">B-cell</a> malignant tumours. This could net MacroGenics up to $700 million.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> In January 2015, the company announced it will utilise <a href="/wiki/Isis_Pharmaceutical" class="mw-redirect" title="Isis Pharmaceutical">Isis Pharmaceuticals</a>' RNA-targeting technology to discover and develop <a href="/wiki/Antisense" class="mw-redirect" title="Antisense">antisense</a> drugs targeting autoimmune disorders of the <a href="/wiki/Gastrointestinal_tract" title="Gastrointestinal tract">gastrointestinal tract</a>, with the partnership potentially generating up to $835 million for Isis.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> In May 2018, Janssen announced it would acquire BeneVir Biopharm, Inc. for an undisclosed sum.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p><p>In December 2019 XBiotech Inc. announced it would sell its novel antibody treatment (<a href="/wiki/Bermekimab" title="Bermekimab">bermekimab</a>) that neutralizes <a href="/wiki/Interleukin-1" class="mw-redirect" title="Interleukin-1">interleukin-1</a> alpha (IL-1⍺) to Janssen Biotech, Inc. for $750 million plus up to a further $600 million.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Ethicon.2C_Inc."></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethicon,_Inc.">Ethicon, Inc.</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnson_%26_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Ethicon, Inc." data-section="9" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 1915, <a href="/wiki/George_F._Merson" title="George F. Merson">George F. Merson</a> opened a facility in Edinburgh for the manufacturing, packaging and sterilizing of catgut, silk and nylon sutures. Johnson &amp; Johnson acquired Mr. Merson's company in 1947, and this was renamed Ethicon Suture Laboratories.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> In 1953 this became Ethicon Inc.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> In 1992, Ethicon was restructured, and <a href="/wiki/Ethicon_Endo-Surgery,_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="Ethicon Endo-Surgery, Inc.">Ethicon Endo-Surgery, Inc.</a> became a separate corporation. During the 1990s, Ethicon diversified into new and advanced products and technologies and formed four different companies under the Ethicon umbrella, each of which specializes in different products.
</p><p>In 2008 J&amp;J announced it would acquire <a href="/wiki/Mentor_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Mentor Corporation">Mentor Corporation</a> for $1 billion and merge its operations into Ethicon.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> In the same year, Ethicon acquired Omrix Biopharmaceuticals, Inc. for $25 per share,<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> or $438 million in total.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> In May 2012 Johnson &amp; Johnson (China) Investment Ltd announced it would acquire surgery blood clotting developer, Guangzhou Bioseal Biotechnology Co., Ltd.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> In March 2016, J&amp;Js Ethicon business unit announced it would acquire NeuWave Medical, Inc.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> In January 2017, J&amp;J subsidiary Ethicon announced it would acquire Megadyne Medical Products, Inc., a medical device company that develops, manufactures and markets electrosurgical tools.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> In February 2017, Ethicon acquired medical device manufacturer, Torax Medical for an undisclosed sum.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> In June 2018, the business announced that Advanced Sterilization Products would be sold off to <a href="/wiki/Fortive_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Fortive Corporation">Fortive Corporation</a> for around $2.8 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p><p>In February 2019, Johnson &amp; Johnson announced that Ethicon had agreed to acquire surgical robotic company, Auris Health Inc, for $3.4 billion in cash<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> and over $2.3 billion in contingent payments based on performance.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> In December of the same year, the company announced it would acquire the portion of Verb Surgical Inc, that it did not already own, from Verily, Alphabet's life sciences division.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span id="Ethicon_Endo-Surgery.2C_Inc."></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethicon_Endo-Surgery,_Inc.">Ethicon Endo-Surgery, Inc.</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnson_%26_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Ethicon Endo-Surgery, Inc." data-section="10" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ethicon_Endo-Surgery" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethicon Endo-Surgery">Ethicon Endo-Surgery</a> was part of Ethicon Inc. until 1992, when it became a separate corporate entity under the J&amp;J umbrella. In 2008 Ethicon Endo-Surgery acquired tissue sealing system developer, SurgRx, Inc.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> In September 2011 the business acquired SterilMed, Inc.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Actelion">Actelion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnson_%26_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Actelion" data-section="11" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In January 2017, J&amp;J fought off competition from <a href="/wiki/Sanofi" title="Sanofi">Sanofi</a> to acquire Swiss drugmaker <a href="/wiki/Actelion" title="Actelion">Actelion</a>. Later in the month J&amp;J announced a $30 billion deal, the largest ever pursued by the company,<sup id="cite_ref-:0_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-56">[56]</a></sup> to purchase the Swiss company <a href="/wiki/Actelion" title="Actelion">Actelion</a> and to spin off its research and development unit, into a separate legal entity.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wsj-rockoff_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj-rockoff-58">[58]</a></sup> In March, the company declared its tender offer for Swiss biotechnology company Actelion successful on Friday, reporting that Janssen Holding GmbH controlled 77.2 percent of the voting rights after the main offer period,<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> equating to 83,195,346 Actelion shares. In keeping with earlier agreements, the company announced its intention to delist Actelion, whilst spinning out its drug discovery operations and early-stage clinical development assets into a newly created Swiss-based biopharmaceutical company, Idorsia Ltd.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> J&amp;J will control 16% of Idorsia, with the ability to raise their stake to 32% through convertible notes.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Johnson_.26_Johnson_Vision_Care.2C_Inc."></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Johnson_&amp;_Johnson_Vision_Care,_Inc.">Johnson &amp; Johnson Vision Care, Inc.</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnson_%26_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Johnson &amp; Johnson Vision Care, Inc." data-section="12" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In July 2016, J&amp;J announced its intention to acquire the privately held company, Vogue International LLC, boosting Johnson &amp; Johnson Consumer Inc.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> In September of the same year, J&amp;J announced it would acquire <a href="/wiki/Abbott_Laboratories" title="Abbott Laboratories">Abbott Medical Optics</a> from <a href="/wiki/Abbott_Laboratories" title="Abbott Laboratories">Abbott Laboratories</a> for $4.325 billion, adding the new division into Johnson &amp; Johnson Vision Care, Inc.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p><p>In July 2017, Johnson &amp; Johnson Vision Care, Inc announced that its Abbott Medical Optics subsidiary would acquire <a href="/wiki/TearScience" title="TearScience">TearScience</a>, who recently received FDA approval for an office-based approach to imaging <a href="/wiki/Meibomian_glands" class="mw-redirect" title="Meibomian glands">meibomian glands</a> and treating <a href="/wiki/Meibomian_gland_dysfunction" class="mw-redirect" title="Meibomian gland dysfunction">meibomian gland dysfunction</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> In September, the company acquired subscription-based contact lens startup Sightbox.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p><p>In 2019, Johnson &amp; Johnson announced the release of photochromic contact lenses. The lenses adjust to sunlight and help eyes recover from bright light exposure faster. The lenses contain a photochromic additive that adapts visible light amounts filtered to the eyes and are the first to use such additives.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="2010_onwards">2010 onwards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnson_%26_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 2010 onwards" data-section="13" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In October 2010, J&amp;J acquired <a href="/wiki/Crucell" title="Crucell">Crucell</a> for $2.4 billion<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> and will operate as the centre for vaccines, within the wider Johnson &amp; Johnson pharmaceuticals group.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p><p>In November 2015, Biosense Webster, Inc. acquired Coherex, Medical Inc. expanding the companies range of treatment options for patients with <a href="/wiki/Atrial_fibrillation" title="Atrial fibrillation">atrial fibrillation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p><p>In March 2018, the company announced that <a href="/wiki/LifeScan,_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="LifeScan, Inc.">LifeScan, Inc.</a> would be sold off to <a href="/wiki/Platinum_Equity" title="Platinum Equity">Platinum Equity</a> for around $2.1 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> In September of the same year Johnson &amp; Johnson Medical GmbH acquired Emerging Implant Technologies GmbH, manufacturer of 3D-printed titanium interbody implants for spinal fusion surgery.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Structure">Structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnson_%26_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Structure" data-section="14" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(2)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Finance">Finance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnson_%26_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Finance" data-section="15" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-2 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-2">
<p>For the fiscal year 2018, Johnson &amp; Johnson reported earnings of US$15.3 billion, with an annual revenue of US$81.6 billion, an increase of 6.7% over the previous fiscal cycle. Johnson &amp; Johnson's shares traded at over $126 per share, and its market capitalization was valued at over US$367.5 billion in September 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>

<p>Current members of the board of directors of Johnson &amp; Johnson for 2019 are: Alex Gorsky, Mary C. Beckerle, D. Scott Davis, Ian E. L. Davis, Jennifer A. Doudna, Mark B. McClellan, Anne M. Mulcahy, William D. Perez, Charles Prince, A. Eugene Washington, Marillyn A. Hewson and Ronald A. Williams.<sup id="cite_ref-Johnson_&amp;_Johnson_Board_of_Directors_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Johnson_&amp;_Johnson_Board_of_Directors-74">[74]</a></sup></p><p>Current members of Executive Committees of Johnson &amp; Johnson are: Joseph Wolk (the company's <a href="/wiki/Chief_financial_officer" title="Chief financial officer">chief financial officer</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-:0_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-56">[56]</a></sup> Peter Fasolo, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Stoffels" title="Paul Stoffels">Paul Stoffels</a>, and Michael Sneed.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p><p>On July 2, 2018, Johnson &amp; Johnson's head of pharmaceuticals, Joaquin Duato, became the vice chairman of the executive committee.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(4)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Chairmen">Chairmen</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnson_%26_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Chairmen" data-section="17" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-4 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-4">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Robert_Wood_Johnson_I" title="Robert Wood Johnson I">Robert Wood Johnson I</a> (1887–1910)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/James_Wood_Johnson" title="James Wood Johnson">James Wood Johnson</a> (1910–1932)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Robert_Wood_Johnson_II" title="Robert Wood Johnson II">Robert Wood Johnson II</a> (1932–1963)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Philip_B._Hofmann" title="Philip B. Hofmann">Philip B. Hofmann</a> (1963–1973)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Richard_B._Sellars" title="Richard B. Sellars">Richard B. Sellars</a> (1973–1976)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/James_E._Burke" title="James E. Burke">James E. Burke</a> (1976–1989)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ralph_S._Larsen" title="Ralph S. Larsen">Ralph S. Larsen</a> (1989–2002)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/William_C._Weldon" title="William C. Weldon">William C. Weldon</a> (2002–2012)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alex_Gorsky" title="Alex Gorsky">Alex Gorsky</a> (2012–present)</li></ul></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(5)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Headquarters_and_the_New_Brunswick_gentrification">Headquarters and the New Brunswick gentrification</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnson_%26_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Headquarters and the New Brunswick gentrification" data-section="18" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-5 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-5">
<p>The company has historically been located on the <a href="/wiki/Delaware_and_Raritan_Canal" title="Delaware and Raritan Canal">Delaware and Raritan Canal</a> in New Brunswick. The company considered moving its headquarters out of New Brunswick in the 1960s, but decided to stay in the town after city officials promised to revitalize downtown New Brunswick by demolishing old buildings and constructing new ones. While New Brunswick lost many historic structures, including the early home of Rutgers University, and most of its historic commercial waterfront to the redevelopment effort, the gentrification did attract people back to New Brunswick. Johnson &amp; Johnson hired <a href="/wiki/Henry_N._Cobb" title="Henry N. Cobb">Henry N. Cobb</a> from <a href="/wiki/Pei_Cobb_Freed_%26_Partners" title="Pei Cobb Freed &amp; Partners">Pei Cobb Freed &amp; Partners</a> to design its new headquarters. <a href="/wiki/Johnson_and_Johnson_Plaza" title="Johnson and Johnson Plaza">Johnson and Johnson Plaza</a>, in a park across the <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Corridor" title="Northeast Corridor">railroad tracks</a> from the older portion of the headquarters, is one of <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_New_Brunswick" class="mw-redirect" title="List of tallest buildings in New Brunswick">tallest buildings in New Brunswick</a>.
</p><p>The stretch of Delaware and Raritan canal by the company's headquarters was replaced by a stretch of <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Route_18" title="New Jersey Route 18">Route 18</a> in the late 1970s,<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> after a lengthy dispute.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> In 2002, the company released its plan of setting up <a href="/wiki/Asia-Pacific" title="Asia-Pacific">Asia-Pacific</a> information technology headquarters in New South Wales within five years.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(6)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Products">Products</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnson_%26_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Products" data-section="19" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-6 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-6">
<p>The company's business is divided into three major segments, Pharmaceuticals, Medical Devices, and Consumer Products. In 2015, these segments contributed 44.9%, 35.9%, and 19.2%, respectively, of the company's total revenues.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Pharmaceuticals">Pharmaceuticals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnson_%26_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Pharmaceuticals" data-section="20" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The company's major franchises in the Pharmaceutical segment include Immunology, Neuroscience, Infectious Disease, and Oncology.
</p><p>Immunology products include the anti-<a href="/wiki/Tumor_necrosis_factor" class="mw-redirect" title="Tumor necrosis factor">tumor necrosis factor</a> antibodies Remicade (<a href="/wiki/Infliximab" title="Infliximab">infliximab</a>), and Simponi (<a href="/wiki/Golimumab" title="Golimumab">golimumab</a>) used for the treatment<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> of autoimmune diseases, including <a href="/wiki/Rheumatoid_arthritis" title="Rheumatoid arthritis">rheumatoid arthritis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crohn%27s_disease" title="Crohn's disease">Crohn's disease</a> (Remicade only), <a href="/wiki/Ulcerative_colitis" title="Ulcerative colitis">ulcerative colitis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ankylosing_spondylitis" title="Ankylosing spondylitis">ankylosing spondylitis</a>, and other disorders. In 2013, these two products accounted for 29% of Johnson and Johnson's pharmaceutical revenues, and 11.3% of the company's total revenues. A third immunology product, Stelara (<a href="/wiki/Ustekinumab" title="Ustekinumab">ustekinumab</a>), targets <a href="/wiki/Interleukin-12" class="mw-redirect" title="Interleukin-12">interleukin-12</a> and <a href="/wiki/Interleukin-23" class="mw-redirect" title="Interleukin-23">interleukin-23</a> and is used for the treatment of <a href="/wiki/Psoriasis" title="Psoriasis">psoriasis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p><p>The company's CNS products include the ADHD drug Concerta (<a href="/wiki/Methylphenidate" title="Methylphenidate">methylphenidate</a> extended release), and the long-acting injectable antipsychotics Invega Sustenna (<a href="/wiki/Paliperidone_palmitate" class="mw-redirect" title="Paliperidone palmitate">paliperidone palmitate</a>) and Risperdal Consta (<a href="/wiki/Risperidone" title="Risperidone">risperidone</a>). Invega Sustenna and Risperdal Consta were the first widely utilized long-acting depot injections for the treatment of schizophrenia. Designed to address the issue of poor patient compliance with oral therapy, they are administered by intramuscular injection at intervals of 2 weeks and one month, respectively. Only minimal improvements in outcomes relative to the oral versions of these drugs were observed in the clinical trial setting, but some evidence suggests that the advantages of long-acting injections in clinical practice may be greater than is readily demonstrated in the environment of a clinical trial.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p><p>Oncology products include Velcade (<a href="/wiki/Bortezomib" title="Bortezomib">bortezomib</a>), for the treatment of multiple myeloma and mantle cell lymphoma<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> and Zytiga (<a href="/wiki/Abiraterone" title="Abiraterone">abiraterone</a>), an androgen antagonist for the treatment of prostate cancer. In clinical trials, abiraterone treatment was associated with a 4.6 to 5.2 survival advantage when used either before or after chemotherapy with platinum-based drugs.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> On December 31, 2012, the <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Drug_Administration" title="Food and Drug Administration">Food and Drug Administration</a> approved <a href="/wiki/Bedaquiline" title="Bedaquiline">Sirturo</a> (bedaquiline), a Johnson &amp; Johnson <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a> drug that is the first new medicine to fight the infection in more than forty years.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p><p>Historically notable drugs include Incivio (<a href="/wiki/Telaprevir" title="Telaprevir">telaprevir</a>) for treating <a href="/wiki/Hepatitis_C" title="Hepatitis C">hepatitis C</a>, whose sales declined from $2.4 billion in 2014 to $106 million in 2016 as competing curative drugs emerged.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> HIV drugs include Edurant (<a href="/wiki/Rilpivirine" title="Rilpivirine">rilpivirine</a>), Intelence (<a href="/wiki/Etravirine" title="Etravirine">etravirine</a>) and Prezista (<a href="/wiki/Darunavir" title="Darunavir">darunavir</a>) but as of 2018, the most significant of these only accounted for around 2% of total revenue at $211 million.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></p><p>In March 2019 the FDA approved <a href="/wiki/Esketamine" title="Esketamine">esketamine</a> for the treatment of severe depression,<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> which is marketed as Spravato by Janssen Pharmaceuticals.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Medical_devices">Medical devices</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnson_%26_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Medical devices" data-section="21" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Sectors in which the company is active<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> include:
</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">
<ul><li>Aesthetics (Ethicon, Mentor)</li>
<li>Arrhythmias (Biosense Webster)</li>
<li>Bariatric Surgery for Obesity (Ethicon)</li>
<li>Cardiovascular Disease (Biosense Webster, Inc.)</li>
<li>Diabetes Care (LifeScan, Animas Corporation)</li>
<li>Ear, Nose, and Throat Conditions (Acclarent)</li>
<li>General Surgery (Ethicon, Codman Neuro)</li>

<li>Self-Measured Blood Glucose Monitors (LifeScan)</li>

<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Consumer_health">Consumer health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Johnson_%26_Johnson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Consumer health" data-section="22" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
